You should not throw lobsters from a boat when putting them back in the water. Here are the reasons why:  1. **Injury Risk**: Throwing lobsters can injure them. They have hard exoskeletons, but their internal organs are delicate. The impact with the water surface from a height can cause trauma.  2. **Proper Orientation**: Lobsters need to enter the water in a way that allows them to orient themselves quickly. Gently lowering them ensures they can right themselves and start moving immediately.  3. **Stress Reduction**: Lobsters are already stressed from being out of their natural environment. Throwing them can increase their stress levels, which can negatively impact their health and chances of survival.  4. **Conservation Practices**: Best practices for marine conservation suggest gently returning animals to their habitat to minimize harm and ensure their well-being.  Instead, gently place lobsters back into the water close to the surface, ensuring they can swim away safely. This method helps ensure their survival and reduces the risk of injury.
